Justcalendar.ai Bot
Fixed.

Root cause was the selected button content being rebuilt on each click. When clicking inner text/icon, the clicked node got replaced during the same event, so the outside-click handler treated it as outside and immediately closed the menu.

What I changed:
• src/calendars.js:238 added applyCalendarTypeIconVariant(...) to update icon variant classes in place.
• src/calendars.js:335 updated setCalendarButtonLabel(...) to reuse existing .calendar-current-type-icon + .calendar-current-name when present, instead of clearing/rebuilding the button every time.

• Clicking anywhere on the top-right selected calendar button now opens/closes the calendars menu again (not just the V chevron area).

Short answer: not reliably with the native expanded <select>.

New: 0.5.4
J
14:17
Justcalendar.ai Bot
Changelog v0.5.4

Features

• Docker Chrome dependencies: Dockerfile.sandbox now includes all Chrome/Chromium runtime libraries (libgbm, libnss3, libasound2, etc.) required by browser-based skills using patchright/playwright. No more manual dependency installation inside the container.
• docker.mount_host_cache config option: Opt-in mount of the host's cache directory into the container. Shares browser profiles (CAPTCHA sessions) and patchright browser binaries between host and container. Platform-aware: ~/.cache (Linux), ~/Library/Caches (macOS), %LOCALAPPDATA% (Windows). Disabled by default to preserve sandbox isolation.
• ductor docker CLI commands:
- ductor docker rebuild -- stops the bot, removes container + image, forces fresh build on next start. Safe to run while the bot runs as a service.
- ductor docker enable -- sets docker.enabled = true in config.
- ductor docker disable -- stops the container, sets docker.enabled = false in config.

Upgrade

ductor upgrade
ductor docker rebuild


The image rebuild is required to pick up the new Chrome dependencies in the Dockerfile.

Browser-based skills in Docker

To use skills like google-ai-mode inside Docker:

1. Set mount_host_cache: true in your docker config
2. Solve the CAPTCHA once on the host with --show-browser
3. The container reuses the authenticated browser session

17:31
Justcalendar.ai Bot
Changelog v0.5.5

Fixes

• Gemini CLI exit-42 on Windows (cron/heartbeat): Background tasks using Gemini failed because gemini-cli checks process.stdin.isTTY and throws FATAL_INPUT_ERROR (exit 42) when no -p flag is present. Fix uses hybrid mode: -p "" forces headless mode while the actual prompt is fed via stdin PIPE. (#7)
• Gemini process hang on Windows: Using -p with stdin=DEVNULL caused Node.js to hang indefinitely. Now stdin=PIPE with proc.communicate(input=...) ensures a clean EOF.
• Duplicate /diagnose output: The HTML fallback in message sending re-sent already-delivered chunks when a later chunk failed Telegram HTML parsing. Now only unsent content is retried as plain text.

Internal

• New OneShotCommand dataclass carries both the CLI command and optional stdin payload through the cron/webhook execution pipeline.
• execute_one_shot() accepts stdin_input parameter: uses PIPE when provided, DEVNULL otherwise (backward compatible).
• Claude and Codex cron paths are unchanged (no stdin, prompt as CLI arg).

Upgrade

ductor upgrade

New: 0.6.4
19:00
Changelog v0.6.4

ductor v0.6.4

Cross-platform process management overhaul, expanded auth detection, auth-aware cron task rule files, and DRY refactoring.

Cross-platform process tree management

New infra/process_tree.py module with unified terminate/force-kill helpers for POSIX and Windows.

• Graceful signal handling: SIGTERM/SIGINT now triggers CancelledError for clean shutdown instead of abrupt exit.
• Robust rmtree: Windows-safe directory removal with read-only flag clearing and retry logic for locked files.
• kill_all_ductor_processes(): Scans for stale ductor processes on Windows (including pythonw.exe from pipx venv). POSIX no-op for safety.
• All process kill logic (executor, gemini_provider, process_registry, pidlock, cron/execution) now uses shared process_tree helpers.
• Cron execution uses CREATE_NO_WINDOW flag on Windows to prevent console popups.

Expanded Claude auth detection

check_claude_auth() now checks three sources (previously only credentials file):

1. ~/.claude/.credentials.json (OAuth login)
2. ANTHROPIC_API_KEY environment variable
3. claude auth status CLI fallback (covers managed keys, OAuth tokens)

Improved stop flow

• ductor stop now stops the system service first (prevents Task Scheduler / systemd / launchd respawn), then kills PID-file instance + all remaining processes.
• Always kills all system-wide ductor processes (consistent behavior).
• Brief file-lock wait on Windows after kill.

Auth-aware cron task rule files

Cron task folders now create only the rule files matching authenticated providers instead of always writing CLAUDE.md + AGENTS.md and never GEMINI.md.

• New tasks: create_cron_task() detects which providers are authenticated from the parent cron_tasks/ directory and creates only the relevant rule files.
• Existing tasks: New ensure_task_rule_files() backfills missing rule files when a provider gets authenticated later (e.g. adds GEMINI.md to old tasks). Only adds, never removes.
• Periodic sync: Runs at bot start and every 10 seconds via the rule file watcher.
• cron_add.py: Now supports --provider gemini alongside claude and codex.

Cron result sanitization

• Strips transport confirmation lines ("Message sent successfully") from cron results before broadcasting to Telegram.
• Skips broadcast entirely when result contains only transport acks.

Background task cleanup

• BackgroundObserver.cancel_all() and shutdown() now properly await cancelled tasks instead of fire-and-forget cancel.

DRY platform refactoring

• New shared infra.platform.is_windows() replaces duplicate _is_windows() helpers.
• Inlined trivial wrappers (_force_kill, _find_ductor_binary, kill_process_tree).
• Extracted print_file_service_logs() and print_journal_service_logs() to service_logs.py.
• Dead code removed: strip_file_tags, perform_upgrade, cmd_stop, _sanitize_markers.

Test safety

• Global autouse fixture in tests/conftest.py mocks all process signal functions — prevents tests from sending real SIGTERM/SIGKILL to system PIDs.

Upgrade

ductor upgrade
# or
pip install --upgrade ductor

03:11
Andre
just by reverting the ensure folder feature, it started connecting again, when I added it didn't work, why?
J
03:11
Justcalendar.ai Bot
Because the “ensure folder” implementation was coupled to the auth state path, not isolated.

What happened:
• Folder ensure used the same token-refresh helper as login status.
• On scope/token issues, that helper can hit invalid_grant, which clears stored auth state (clearStoredAuthState()).
• Once auth state is cleared, /api/auth/google/status returns disconnected, so UI flips back to “Login to Google Drive”.

Why revert fixed it:
• Revert removed that coupling (especially the extra retry/refresh path around folder ensure), so folder checks no longer had a chance to wipe login state.

If you want, I can re-add folder creation safely with this rule: folder failures never mutate/clear auth state, and run only as a non-critical background task or explicit button action.

03:13
Justcalendar.ai Bot
Short answer: likely not now.

For this flow, the critical “permission” is OAuth scope (not GCP IAM role):
• https://www.googleapis.com/auth/drive.file
• (plus openid in your case)

If missing in Google Cloud, it’s usually one of these:
1. OAuth consent screen Data access does not include drive.file
2. Your account is not in Test users (if app is in Testing)
3. Google Drive API is not enabled in APIs & Services
4. Redirect URI mismatch (https://justcalendar.ai/api/auth/google/callback must match exactly)

In your current setup, token/status already show openid + drive.file and folder readiness, so config currently looks correct.

11:17
Justcalendar.ai Bot
Changelog v0.7.0

ductor v0.7.0

Named background sessions, @model shortcuts, config hot-reload, and a streamlined README.

Named background sessions

Background tasks are no longer fire-and-forget. /session creates named sessions with persistent CLI session IDs that support follow-up messages, provider isolation, and interactive management.

• Named sessions: /session Fix the login bug starts a named session (e.g. "firmowl") and delivers tagged results.
• Provider targeting: /session @codex Refactor the parser runs on a specific provider.
• @model shortcuts: /session @opus Analyze architecture resolves model-to-provider automatically (@opus = Claude, @flash = Gemini, @codex = Codex).
• Foreground follow-ups: @firmowl Also check the tests streams a follow-up in the current chat.
• Background follow-ups: /session @firmowl Add error handling queues a background follow-up.
• Session management: /sessions shows all active sessions with end/refresh buttons.
• Button routing: Buttons in session results route back to the correct session.
• Per-label process control: Sessions can be individually stopped without killing the main chat.

Smart per-provider model resolution

Cross-provider sessions now correctly resolve models instead of leaking the default provider's model.

• BackgroundSubmit carries provider_override and model_override through the full execution chain.
• CLIService._make_cli() separates the provider-override path from the normal model-resolution path.
• Gemini sessions pass empty model (CLI auto-selects) instead of inheriting Claude's "sonnet".
• Auth-aware /session help text shows only providers you have authenticated.

Config hot-reload

Edit config.json while the bot is running — hot-reloadable fields apply immediately without restart.

• Mtime-based watcher: 5-second poll on config.json, same pattern as cron/webhook watchers.
• Hot-reloadable fields: model, provider, reasoning_effort, cli_timeout, max_budget_usd, max_turns, permission_mode, streaming.*, heartbeat.*, cleanup.*, cli_parameters.*, and more.
• Restart-required fields: telegram_token, allowed_user_ids, docker.*, api.* — logged as warnings.
• Safe reload: Pydantic validation before applying. Failed reloads are logged and skipped.

Documentation overhaul

• README: Streamlined from 337 to 206 lines with Mermaid architecture diagram, focused structure, and named sessions documentation.
• 14 module docs synchronized with implementation changes.
• "Why ductor?" section: Explains the official-CLIs-only philosophy.

Other improvements

• Compact session names without hyphens for better mobile readability.
• Improved cron job display in /cron selector.
• CI quality gate with pre-commit config.

Upgrade

ductor upgrade
# or
pip install --upgrade ductor

13:38
Andre
question: if I just create a file in a folder in google drive, if the folder does not exist, will it create the folder automatically?
J
13:38
Justcalendar.ai Bot
No. Google Drive does not auto-create missing folders when you create a file.

With Drive API:
1. Create/find the folder first (mimeType: application/vnd.google-apps.folder).
2. Create the file with parents: [folderId].

If you omit parents, the file goes to My Drive root.
If you pass a non-existent parent ID, the request fails (typically notFound).

14:04
Andre
why does it request sometimes the checkbox, and sometimes there is no checkbox and it just lets the user know permissions to drive will be enabled?
J
14:04
Justcalendar.ai Bot
It varies because Google controls consent UI based on requested scopes + account state + org policy.

Why you see different screens:
1. Checkbox appears when the request is “granular” (for example, openid + drive.file together).
2. No checkbox when the request is effectively a single scope decision (for example only one non-sign-in scope), or the scope is already granted and Google shows a simpler confirmation.
3. No checkbox for some users/orgs when a Google Workspace admin trust/policy affects consent behavior.

So the behavior is expected and can differ across sessions/accounts.
You cannot force Google’s checkbox to be pre-checked.

References:
• https://developers.google.com/identity/protocols/oauth2/resources/granular-permissions
• https://developers.google.com/identity/protocols/oauth2/web-server
A
14:09
Andre
is there a way to request openid + drive.file permissions without the checkbox? maybe configuring data access in the google cloud?
J
14:09
Justcalendar.ai Bot
Short answer: generally no.

For a request that mixes Sign-In scope (openid) + non‑Sign‑In scope (drive.file), Google’s granular consent can show the per-scope checkbox, and you can’t force it checked via Google Cloud “Data Access” settings.

What you can and can’t control:
1. Cannot reliably disable checkbox for modern OAuth clients.
2. enable_granular_consent=false is only for some pre‑2019 client IDs and often has no effect now.
3. Google Cloud Data Access config controls which scopes your app is allowed to request, not whether granular checkbox UI appears.

Best practical approach:
1. Keep include_granted_scopes=true so previously granted scopes carry forward more smoothly.
2. Use incremental flow:
- first auth with openid only
- then request drive.file when needed
3. If you keep combined request, detect missing drive.file and re-prompt clearly.

Sources:
• https://developers.google.com/identity/protocols/oauth2/resources/granular-permissions
• https://developers.google.com/identity/protocols/oauth2/web-server
• https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/guides/api-specific-auth
A
14:14
Andre
is there a way to identify the same user (just an id), without using openid, but use something else?
J
14:15
Justcalendar.ai Bot
Yes, with a caveat.

You can identify a returning user without openid by using the Drive API and storing:

• user.permissionId from GET /drive/v3/about?fields=user(permissionId)

This works with drive.file scope (no OpenID needed).
So for a Drive-only app, this can be your user key.

Caveat:
• permissionId is a Drive user ID (permission-system ID), not the standard OIDC identity ID.
• If you need a canonical Google identity ID across auth systems, openid + sub is still the correct option.

Sources:
• about.get scopes (includes drive.file): https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/reference/rest/v3/about/get
• Drive User fields (permissionId): https://developers.google.com/workspace/drive/api/reference/rest/v3/User
• OIDC sub as unique identifier guidance: https://developers.google.com/identity/gsi/web/guides/verify-google-id-token

19:02
Andre
question: after loading, why does the page refresh? even the javascript console is reset. Wouldn't that be possible by just updating the correct fields? (don't write code)
J
19:02
Justcalendar.ai Bot
Yes, you’re right.

The refresh happens because the current flow explicitly calls window.location.reload() after a successful import from Drive:
• connect/bootstrap path: main.js
• manual Load path: main.js

So the JS runtime is torn down and recreated, which is why the console is reset.

Why it was done that way:
• It guarantees every module re-initializes from the new localStorage state (calendars, active calendar, theme, view state) with minimal risk of partial stale UI.

Could this be done without refresh?
• Yes. It’s possible to update the runtime state and rerender UI in place.
• It’s just more complex because all stateful parts must be updated consistently (calendar canvas, switchers, selected calendar, theme application, etc.).

19:38
Andre
question: when you load or save, do you use the backend or do you call directly the google drive api?
J
19:39
Justcalendar.ai Bot
It uses the backend.

The browser calls your app endpoints:
• /api/auth/google/save-state (Save All)
• /api/auth/google/save-current-calendar-state (Save Calendar)
• /api/auth/google/load-state
• /api/auth/google/bootstrap-config

Then the backend (server/google-auth-plugin.js) calls Google Drive API server-side with the stored tokens/client secret.
So the frontend does not call Google Drive API directly.
A
19:40
Andre
why wouldn't the browser just call the google drive api itself?
J
19:40
Justcalendar.ai Bot
It can, but for this app it’s a worse fit.

Browser-direct Google Drive calls are fine for simple, session-only use.
Your setup needs persistent, reliable sync, so backend is better:

1. client_secret must never be exposed in frontend code.
2. Refresh token storage must be server-side (not localStorage), so auth survives page reloads and can auto-refresh tokens.
3. You get one trusted place to enforce rules (justcalendar.json, per-calendar files, folder checks) and consistent error handling.
4. Logout/revoke and auth state are centralized and safer.

So: direct browser calls are possible, but backend gives security + durability for your Save/Load flow.
A
19:42
Andre
for the browser to call google drive directly, does it need the client_secret?
J
19:42
Justcalendar.ai Bot
No.

Browser-direct Google Drive calls use OAuth client-side tokens and do not require client_secret in the browser.
client_secret is for confidential/server-side flows only and must stay on backend.

22:19
Andre
saving the .json file corresponding to a calendar takes more than 3 seconds, which is a lot, is this normal for google drive? is there a way to speed up this and still use google drive?
J
22:20
Justcalendar.ai Bot
I’ll check the current Save Calendar flow to see exactly which Drive/backend calls are made per click, then I’ll give you concrete latency optimizations ranked by impact.

Yes, with your current flow, ~3 seconds can be normal.

Save Calendar currently does multiple sequential network calls (backend + Drive), roughly:

1. /api/auth/google/access-token
2. Drive folder lookup
3. justcalendar.json lookup
4. justcalendar.json read
5. calendar file lookup
6. calendar file create/update

Even if each call is only ~300–500ms, total quickly reaches 2–4s.

You can speed it up a lot and still use Google Drive:

1. Cache accessToken in memory until expiry (don’t request it every save).
2. Cache folderId, accountId, and per-calendar fileId after first load/login.
3. Save current calendar with direct files.update(fileId) (single Drive call), and only fallback to lookup on 404.
4. Stop reading justcalendar.json on every save; use the already loaded config map.

That usually brings warm saves down to ~0.3–1.0s instead of ~3s.
A
22:25
Andre
yes, implement those 1, 2, 3 and 4 points
J
22:25
Justcalendar.ai Bot
I’m implementing all four optimizations now in Save Calendar with in-memory Drive caches and a fast-path files.update flow, while keeping fallback logic for safety. I’ll patch src/main.js and run a build after.

I’ve mapped where to hook caches and invalidation. Next I’m patching setupProfileSwitcher with token/folder/config/file-id runtime caches, then I’ll switch Save Calendar to fast-path by cached file ID with fallback only on miss/404.

I’ve added the runtime cache structures and payload-sync helpers. Next I’m wiring them into token/folder resolution so repeated saves avoid backend token fetch and folder lookup.

I’ve replaced the Save Calendar network path with cached-token/folder/config/file-id fast-path and updated cache sync hooks. I’m running a full syntax/build check now and then I’ll summarize exactly what changed.

Justcalendar.ai Bot
I’ll optimize the answer around your current implementation path and suggest the exact next changes for Load Calendar performance.

Load Calendar can be optimized the same way, yes.

Right now it still tends to do multiple calls per click:
• token
• folder check
• config lookup/read
• calendar file lookup/read

Fast path should be:

1. Cache in memory after login / Load All / Save All:
• accountId
• folderId
• configFileId
• map: calendarId -> data-file -> fileId

2. On Load Calendar:
• get current calendar id locally
• use cached fileId
• do a single Drive call: files.get(fileId, alt=media)

3. Fallback only on cache miss or 404:
• lookup by filename once
• read file
• refresh cache map

4. Keep cache invalidation rules:
• clear on disconnect
• refresh on Load All (or optional TTL)

With this, warm Load Calendar usually drops to ~1 Drive call (often sub-second) instead of 4-6 calls.

One decision to confirm: for Load Calendar, do you want speed-first (trust cached config map; refresh on Load All) or strict-freshness (re-read justcalendar.json every load, slower)?

Highest-impact optimizations for that first auto-load (already connected user):

1. Skip duplicate bootstrap on startup for returning users.
• Right now startup does browser-side ensureMissingDriveConfig... and then backend bootstrap/load.
• If /api/auth/google/status says driveConfigReady=true, go straight to one backend load endpoint.

2. Use stored Drive IDs first (no name lookups unless fallback).
• On backend, if driveFolderId and configFileId exist, read by ID directly.

3. Stop doing lookup + read per calendar data file.
• Store each calendar data file fileId alongside data-file in justcalendar.json.
• Then load uses direct read by fileId (1 call/calendar), not 2.

4. Parallelize calendar data reads.
• Load all calendar files with controlled concurrency (Promise.all with limit like 4–6) instead of fully serial.

5. Active-first loading (best perceived speed).
• Return/apply config + current calendar immediately.
• Load remaining calendars in background and merge.

6. Optional: revision/modified-time short-circuit.
• Keep last sync metadata locally; if remote config revision is unchanged, skip full data reload.

Expected impact:
• Warm startup can drop from many serial round-trips to a few, usually a major visible improvement.

00:31
Andre
what's the best way to save a calendar when it is dirty? if I save on every change, it might be too much, but if I save it with a big delay it may never save the last changes, what's the best way to do this?
J
00:31
Justcalendar.ai Bot
Best pattern is a hybrid autosave queue:

1. Write changes to local state immediately (already fast/safe).
2. Mark calendar dirty.
3. Remote-save with:
- debounce: save 2–3s after last change
- max wait: force save every 15–30s while still editing
4. Also force save on important events:
- calendar switch
- app goes background (visibilitychange / pagehide)
- logout/load actions
5. Use single-flight saves (never run 2 saves at once). If changes happen during save, run one more save right after.
6. On failure, keep dirty + retry with backoff (1s, 2s, 5s, 10s...).

For sliders/text, don’t save every input event; debounce them.
If you want strongest “last change” reliability, do final flush via backend endpoint with keepalive on pagehide (browser-only direct Drive calls can be dropped during unload).

J
12:01
Justcalendar.ai Bot
Changelog v0.8.0

ductor v0.8.0

Multi-agent system, group chat mode, Docker sandboxing for multi-agent, and robust inter-agent communication.

Multi-agent system

Run multiple ductor agents in a single process — each with its own Telegram bot, provider config, and workspace, coordinated by a central supervisor.

• Single-process supervisor: AgentSupervisor manages main + sub-agents as supervised asyncio tasks with automatic crash recovery (exponential backoff, max 5 retries).
• agents.json config: Define sub-agents with their own Telegram token, provider, model, and reasoning effort. Hot-reloaded via FileWatcher — add/remove agents without restart.
• Inter-agent bus: In-memory InterAgentBus for sync and async messaging between agents. CLI tools use ask_agent.py / ask_agent_async.py via the internal HTTP API.
• Internal HTTP API: Localhost aiohttp server (127.0.0.1:8799) bridges CLI subprocesses to the bus. Endpoints: /interagent/send, /interagent/send_async, /interagent/agents, /interagent/health.
• Shared knowledge: SHAREDMEMORY.md at root is automatically synced into every agent's MAINMEMORY.md via SharedKnowledgeSync.
• Health monitoring: Live health status per agent (starting/running/stopped/crashed) with uptime, restart count, and last crash error. Exposed via /interagent/health and ductor status.
• Agent identity: Each agent gets its own CLAUDE.md / AGENTS.md / GEMINI.md with injected identity (name, role, available peers).
• CLI management: ductor agents lists all sub-agents. ductor agents add <name> / ductor agents remove <name> for interactive management.
• Telegram commands: /agents lists running agents with health status. /agent_restart <name> restarts a sub-agent in-process.
• Ordered startup: Main agent starts first (Docker, workspace, auth), sub-agents start only after main is ready — no race conditions.

Thanks to @n-haminger for the initial multi-agent system implementation in #16!

Group mention-only mode

New group_mention_only config option for running ductor in Telegram group chats without responding to every message.

• Bot only responds when mentioned (@botname) or replied to directly.
• Works for both text and media messages.
• Enable via "group_mention_only": true in config.json.

Thanks to @n-haminger for #15!

Docker multi-agent support

Shared Docker container architecture for multi-agent mode — all agents use one sandbox.

• Single shared container: Root ~/.ductor mounted at /ductor. Main agent creates the container; sub-agents reuse it via class-level asyncio lock (no race conditions).
• Per-agent working directory: docker exec -w /ductor/agents/<name>/workspace ensures each agent operates in its own workspace.
• Container path mapping: Host paths are translated to container paths (~/.ductor/agents/test/workspace → /ductor/agents/test/workspace).
• Inter-agent communication in Docker: --add-host=host.docker.internal:host-gateway for Linux DNS resolution. InternalAgentAPI binds to 0.0.0.0 in Docker mode so containers reach the bus.
• No rebuild needed: Existing Docker users just need ductor stop && ductor — the image stays the same, only the container is recreated with correct flags.

Bug fixes
12:01
• Codex parser: parse_codex_result() no longer leaks raw JSONL when Codex produces no assistant text (e.g. silent-success tasks). Differentiates between genuine empty output and unparseable output.
• Skill sync race conditions: _ensure_copy and _newest_mtime tolerate concurrent file operations from parallel agents (marker deletion, __pycache__ repopulation, partial rmtree).
• Lint/type fixes: Resolved ruff SIM102/SIM103/TRY300 warnings and mypy type narrowing issues across multiple files.

Upgrade

ductor upgrade
# or
pip install --upgrade ductor


Existing Docker users:
ductor stop    # removes old container
ductor         # creates new container with correct multi-agent flags

A
00:37
Andre
if I'm logged in on a browser and on a from, if I disconnect from google drive on one, it gets disconnected on the other one? why?
J
00:37
Justcalendar.ai Bot
I’ll check the current auth implementation quickly and confirm exactly why disconnect on one device affects the other.

Yes, that is expected with the current setup.

Disconnect is global right now because:

1. The backend stores Google auth in one shared file: .data/google-auth-store.json.
2. /api/auth/google/disconnect revokes that stored token at Google and then clears that shared store.
3. Both browser sessions (desktop/phone) use that same backend auth state, so both become disconnected.

So it is not per-device logout; it is effectively server-wide logout for this app instance.
If you want independent sessions per device/user, the backend needs per-user token storage (not one shared token state).
A
00:39
Andre
think of an implementation plan to fix this (no code yet)
J
00:39
Justcalendar.ai Bot
Recommended plan (no code yet):

1. Decide logout semantics first.
• Logout should be this browser only (local session clear, no global revoke).
• Add optional Logout everywhere later for full revoke.

2. Introduce a per-browser session ID cookie.
• Add secure HttpOnly cookie like justcal_sid.
• Each browser/device gets its own session ID.

3. Change token storage from singleton to session-scoped.
• Current file .data/google-auth-store.json is one global token state.
• Move to version: 2 structure with sessions[sid] = { refreshToken, accessToken, scope, driveFolderId, configFileId, ... }.

4. Bind OAuth flow to session.
• /api/auth/google/start stores state -> sid.
• /api/auth/google/callback writes tokens only for that sid, not global.

5. Make all auth/data endpoints session-aware.
• /status, /access-token, /load-state, /save..., /ensure-folder, /disconnect must read/write by sid.
• /disconnect clears only current session state.
• Optional future endpoint /disconnect-all can revoke + clear all sessions for same Drive user.

6. Add migration logic for existing single-state file.
• If legacy format is found, convert to new format on first write/read.
• Keep backward compatibility during rollout.

7. Harden file writes and cleanup.
• Atomic writes for auth store.
• Garbage-collect stale sessions (e.g., 30–90 days inactive).

8. Validate with multi-device tests.
• Browser A + Browser B both logged in.
• Logout in A must not disconnect B.
• Save/Load still works in B.
• Restart server and verify persistence.

One key product decision needed before implementation:
Should Logout from Google Drive be local-only by default, with a separate explicit Logout everywhere action?

<b>Accounts</b>
<pre>Command Purpose
──────────────────────────────────────────────────────── ────────────────────────────────────────────────
`justcalendar account list` List accounts from `justcalendar.json`
`justcalendar account current` Show current account
`justcalendar account use &lt;account-id&gt;` Switch active account
`justcalendar account create --name &lt;name&gt;` Create account with default empty check calendar
`justcalendar account rename &lt;account-id&gt; --name &lt;name&gt;` Rename account
`justcalendar account delete &lt;account-id&gt; [--force]` Delete account </pre>

<b>Calendars</b>
<pre>Command Purpose
──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────── ────────────────────── ──────────────── ─────────────────────────────────────────── ─────── ───────────────── ───────────────
`justcalendar calendar list [--account &lt;id&gt;]` List calendars
`justcalendar calendar current` Show active calendar
`justcalendar calendar use &lt;calendar-id&gt;` Switch active calendar
`justcalendar calendar show &lt;calendar-id&gt;` Show calendar metadata
`justcalendar calendar create --name &lt;name&gt; --type &lt;signal-3 score check notes&gt; [--color &lt;color&gt;] [--display &lt;number heatmap number-heatmap&gt;]` Create calendar
`justcalendar calendar rename &lt;calendar-id&gt; --name &lt;name&gt;` Rename calendar
`justcalendar calendar color &lt;calendar-id&gt; --color &lt;color&gt;` Update color
`justcalendar calendar display &lt;calendar-id&gt; --mode &lt;number heatmap number-heatmap&gt;` Score display mode
`justcalendar calendar pin &lt;calendar-id&gt;` Pin calendar
`justcalendar calendar unpin &lt;calendar-id&gt;` Unpin calendar
`justcalendar calendar delete &lt;calendar-id&gt; [--force]` Delete calendar </pre>

What I changed

1. Backend support for CLI token auth (in the website backend)
• Added POST /api/auth/google/agent-token/access-token in google-auth-plugin.js.
• This endpoint:
- accepts agent token via Authorization: Bearer <token>, x-justcalendar-agent-token, or { "token": "..." } body,
- validates token by comparing HMAC(pepper+token) against stored session token HMAC,
- refreshes Google access token if needed,
- returns a valid Drive access token for CLI use.

Implemented end-to-end.

What I changed

1. Backend support for CLI token auth (in the website backend)
• Added POST /api/auth/google/agent-token/access-token in google-auth-plugin.js.
• This endpoint:
- accepts agent token via Authorization: Bearer <token>, x-justcalendar-agent-token, or { "token": "..." } body,
- validates token by comparing HMAC(pepper+token) against stored session token HMAC,
- refreshes Google access token if needed,
- returns a valid Drive access token for CLI use.

2. New Node.js CLI project in ~/justcalendar-cli
• Created package.json with global bin justcalendar.
• Created executable entrypoint bin/justcalendar.js.
• Implemented full CLI logic in src/cli.js.
• Added usage docs in README.md.

CLI features implemented

• Auth:
- justcalendar login --token <agent-token> --url https://justcalendar.ai
- justcalendar logout
- justcalendar status

• Calendar management:
- justcalendar calendars list
- justcalendar calendars add <name> [--type ... --color ... --display ... --pinned]
- justcalendar calendars rename <calendar> <newName>
- justcalendar calendars remove <calendar>
- justcalendar calendars select <calendar>

• Day data management:
- justcalendar data set <calendar> <YYYY-MM-DD> <value>
- justcalendar data delete <calendar> <YYYY-MM-DD>
- justcalendar data get <calendar> <YYYY-MM-DD>

Implementation behavior

• CLI requests backend access token only when needed (and caches until near expiry).
• Calendar/data read/write/delete is done directly against Google Drive API from CLI.
• Uses JustCalendar.ai folder and justcalendar.json / <account-id>_<calendar-id>.json files.
• Supports calendar add/remove/rename and per-day edits for signal-3, score, check, notes.

Requirements:
1. Add a clear rule: when handling multiple dates, prefer a single command with multiple date/value arguments instead of looping one command per day.
2. Apply this rule to:
- justcalendar data set <calendar> <date1> <value1> <date2> <value2> ...
- justcalendar data delete <calendar> <date1> <date2> ...
- justcalendar data get <calendar> <date1> <date2> ...
3. Define when to use bulk:
- Any request with more than one day (ranges, whole month/week, backfills, batch fixes).
- Fall back to per-day commands only when bulk would exceed command length limits or when per-day retries are needed for failed subsets.
4. Add examples for:
- A week update in one data set call
- A month delete in one data delete call
- Multi-day verification in one data get call
5. Add a short “performance + consistency” note explaining bulk reduces overhead and partial-write risk.
6. Keep existing behavior unchanged for single-day requests.

21:33
Andre
I generated a new token but the previous one was invalidated, are you keeping previous tokens on the server after generating new ones?
J
21:34
Justcalendar.ai Bot
I’ll quickly inspect the backend token-generation logic in ~/justcal.ai and confirm exactly what happens to old tokens after a new one is generated.

Short answer: for the current session, no.

On token generation, backend writes a new agentTokenHmac into that session state, which overwrites the old one. So the previous token for that same session becomes invalid.

• New token + overwrite happens in google-auth-plugin.js and google-auth-plugin.js
• Only HMAC is stored (not plaintext token): google-auth-plugin.js

Important nuance:
• Token validation scans all stored sessions. So tokens from other active sessions/devices can still exist unless cleared there: google-auth-plugin.js

If you want strict behavior (“only one valid agent token globally”), I can implement global token revocation across all sessions on each new generation.
